| 0:46:38| The Chamber is a membership organization.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CoComWS120917?start=2798)|
| 0:46:43| It's been in existence for over 150 years,| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CoComWS120917?start=2803)|
| 0:46:47| and for this is the 125th year that it's been known as the Knoxville Chamber of Commerce.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CoComWS120917?start=2807)|
| 0:46:54| It has over 2,000 members, most of which are small businesses.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CoComWS120917?start=2814)|
| 0:46:59| Over 50 percent of its members have one to ten employees.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CoComWS120917?start=2819)|
| 0:47:03| Eighty percent of its members have 75 or fewer employees.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CoComWS120917?start=2823)|
| 0:47:08| So it is an organization whose mission is to represent the business community| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CoComWS120917?start=2828)|
| 0:47:14| and to promote regional economic prosperity.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CoComWS120917?start=2834)|
| 0:47:18| The Chamber does that in a number of ways.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CoComWS120917?start=2838)|
| 0:47:21| It has six primary areas of focus.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CoComWS120917?start=2841)|
| 0:47:26| One is new business recruitment.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CoComWS120917?start=2846)|
| 0:47:29| One is small business assistance.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CoComWS120917?start=2849)|
| 0:47:32| One is startup business assistance.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CoComWS120917?start=2852)|
| 0:47:34| It has programs for existing industry.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CoComWS120917?start=2854)|
| 0:47:37| It provides general public services, and it provides government services,| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CoComWS120917?start=2857)|
| 0:47:42| including services to Knox County.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CoComWS120917?start=2862)|
| 0:47:45| The Chamber also has an affiliate known as the Partnership Initiatives Fund,| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CoComWS120917?start=2865)|
| 0:47:51| which carries out some activities of the Chamber that are charitable and educational in nature| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CoComWS120917?start=2871)|
| 0:47:58| and are qualified for charitable deductions under the Internal Revenue Code.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CoComWS120917?start=2878)|
| 0:48:04| The Chamber itself is qualified under Section 501C6 of the Internal Revenue Code.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CoComWS120917?start=2884)|
| 0:48:12| That is a section of the Internal Revenue Code that provides a tax exemption specifically to Chambers of Commerce,| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CoComWS120917?start=2892)|
| 0:48:20| business leagues, trade associations, and other businesses of that type.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CoComWS120917?start=2900)|
| 0:48:26| These organizations are exempt from taxes on their income,| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CoComWS120917?start=2906)|
| 0:48:31| but contributions to them are not charitable contributions.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CoComWS120917?start=2911)|
| 0:48:35| When you think of charitable contributions, you're thinking of a 501C3 corporation,| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CoComWS120917?start=2915)|
| 0:48:41| which is a different type of corporation, different purpose, different requirements,| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CoComWS120917?start=2921)|
| 0:48:47| and qualified under a different section of the Internal Revenue Code.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CoComWS120917?start=2927)|
| 0:48:52| The Partnership Initiatives Fund is a 501C3.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CoComWS120917?start=2932)|
| 0:48:57| The laws applicable to 501C6 organizations and 501C3 organizations are different,| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CoComWS120917?start=2937)|
| 0:49:04| and we'll go through those in just a moment.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CoComWS120917?start=2944)|
| 0:49:08| The Chamber is one of 45 organizations that have defined service agreements with Knox County.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CoComWS120917?start=2948)|

| 1:00:35| And to digress for just a minute, let me give you a quick overview of what the law is on disclosure.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CoComWS120917?start=3635)|
| 1:00:42| There's no law cited in the resolution.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CoComWS120917?start=3642)|
| 1:00:44| There was no law cited at your previous minute.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CoComWS120917?start=3644)|
| 1:00:48| So we went out and reviewed every law that we could think of that was applicable to determine what are they required to disclose.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CoComWS120917?start=3648)|
| 1:00:56| And the answer is this.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CoComWS120917?start=3656)|
| 1:00:58| 501c3 organizations and 501c6 organizations are required to disclose two things.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CoComWS120917?start=3658)|
| 1:01:06| One is their application for exemption from taxes, which the Chamber filed many, many, many years ago.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CoComWS120917?start=3666)|
| 1:01:13| And anybody who wants a copy is welcome to it.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CoComWS120917?start=3673)|
| 1:01:16| And the second is you are required to file your annual tax return, your Form 990,| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CoComWS120917?start=3676)|
| 1:01:22| except federal law specifically provides you are not required to disclose Schedule B.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CoComWS120917?start=3682)|
| 1:01:29| You are not required to disclose contributors, names, addresses, and amounts.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CoComWS120917?start=3689)|
| 1:01:36| And we've given you also a summary of the federal law that clearly delineates what's required, what's not required.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CoComWS120917?start=3696)|
| 1:01:48| Contributors, amounts, and addresses are not included.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CoComWS120917?start=3708)|
| 1:01:53| If you ask the IRS for a copy of the Chambers 990, they will give it to you without that schedule.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CoComWS120917?start=3713)|
| 1:02:00| If you go to GuideStar and look at it, they will give it to you without that schedule.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CoComWS120917?start=3720)|
| 1:02:05| That's because membership organizations and charities consider their donors and members to be a private matter, and it is.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CoComWS120917?start=3725)|
| 1:02:13| And federal law recognizes that.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CoComWS120917?start=3733)|
| 1:02:16| The Code of Federal Regulations confirms it.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CoComWS120917?start=3736)|
| 1:02:20| We looked at state law, and what are the state law requirements?| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CoComWS120917?start=3740)|
| 1:02:23| Well, there's the Public Records Act.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CoComWS120917?start=3743)|
| 1:02:25| It's applicable to state, county, and municipal records.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CoComWS120917?start=3745)|
| 1:02:29| It is not applicable to the Chamber's records.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CoComWS120917?start=3749)|
| 1:02:33| The Chamber is not a governmental entity or agency under any stretch of the law.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CoComWS120917?start=3753)|
| 1:02:39| So the Public Records Act does not apply to the Chamber.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CoComWS120917?start=3759)|
| 1:02:43| There's the Charitable Solicitations Act that does require filings with the state,| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CoComWS120917?start=3763)|
| 1:02:49| but it does not apply to Chambers of Commerce.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CoComWS120917?start=3769)|
| 1:02:52| It only applies to 501C3 charities.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CoComWS120917?start=3772)|
| 1:02:55| And even if it did apply, it doesn't require contributor names, addresses, and donation amounts.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CoComWS120917?start=3775)|
| 1:03:03| It simply requires gross figures of how much you collected.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CoComWS120917?start=3783)|
| 1:03:09| Then there are campaign finance disclosure laws in the state of Tennessee,| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CoComWS120917?start=3789)|
| 1:03:13| but they do not apply to public information campaigns or to matters pending before bodies like county commission.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CoComWS120917?start=3793)|

| 1:03:33| Those two things you have to file a campaign financial disclosure.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CoComWS120917?start=3813)|

| 1:03:41| None of them require the Chamber to disclose these things.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CoComWS120917?start=3821)|
| 1:03:46| Your contract does not require it.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CoComWS120917?start=3826)|
